# Bruno Carrelli  —  *Bruno Carrelli*

![[_attachments/bruno_carrelli.png]]

# Bruno Carrelli — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

**Subject:** Carrelli, Bruno. DOB approx. 1998–1999, Jersey City, NJ. Italian-American, Catholic-cultural, civilian, non-powered, no enhancement, no augmentation, no institutional affiliation beyond academic (Wakandan science academy, post-2017) and employment (Circle Q, Jersey City waterfront, since middle school). No criminal record. No surveillance counter-tradecraft. No threat profile.

**Classification:** Civilian asset, longitudinally indispensable to the Kamala Khan operational theater. Threat-to-self and threat-to-others both negligible. Threat-of-being-quietly-spent-down-by-his-own-architecture: high, chronic, unaddressed.

---

## Bottom Line, Up Front

Bruno Carrelli is a young man who was made into an adult before he was permitted to be a child, and who has organized every subsequent decision of his life around the proposition that *the relationships he values continue to exist only as long as he is the one carrying them*. He is not a hero, not a sidekick, not a victim, and not — despite the temptation of the diagnostic gaze — a case. He is what a particular kind of childhood produces when the temperament is right and the luck holds: a person of exceptional reliability whose reliability is the *symptom* and not the *strength*. He functions. He functions extraordinarily well. The functioning is the problem and also the only thing that has ever been allowed to be the answer.

Strip the file to one sentence: **he loves by building, he grieves by leaving, and he has never in his life made a demand on another person that he could not justify as service to them.**

---

## The Through-Line

The spine of Bruno Carrelli's existence — visible in every era, every relational configuration, every artist's rendering, every writer's hand — is the **conversion of love into infrastructure**. He does not say it. He does not narrate it. He builds it. Kamala needs a suit; he builds the suit. Kamala needs a stabilizer; he builds the stabilizer. Vick needs cover; he provides the cover. Mike needs a boyfriend who shows up; he shows up. Kareem needs a partner who can be present without performance; he is present. Wakanda needs a working scientist; he works. The medium changes; the structure is invariant. Love, for Bruno, is *what you do with your hands while the other person is busy being themselves*. This is why the hand injury (Civil War II, 2016) is not an incident in his biography — it is the *event horizon* of his biography, around which everything before bends inward and everything after orbits at a careful distance.

The through-line, observed across roughly a decade of canon: **eager helper → self-sacrificing infrastructure → silently injured → geographically exiled → professionally reconstituted at one degree of remove.** Each stage is a refinement of the same operation. He does not change strategies. He refines the strategy by absorbing its costs and continuing.

---

## Who He Is at the Deepest Level

A *parentified child whose parentification took*. Most children handed an adult's load too early break in some legible way — acting out, somatizing, depressive collapse, substance use, the predictable rebellions. Bruno did not break. The temperamental endowment was right: high conscientiousness, high agreeableness, strong cognitive control, ethical seriousness uncommon at any age and astonishing at fifteen. The load went on the frame and the frame held. What the file shows, then, is not a broken child but the rarer and more dangerous artifact: the child who *succeeded* at being prematurely adult, and who therefore never had to learn that the role was optional. By the time the role *could* have become optional — late adolescence, the first real chance at a self organized around his own appetites — the role had become identity. There is no Bruno underneath the responsible one. There is only the responsible one, and the very faint outline, visible mostly in the artists' choices around his eyes, of someone who once briefly considered being someone else and decided it would inconvenience others.

At the deepest level he is **a person who experiences his own desires as a kind of rudeness**. Not as shameful, not as forbidden — as *impolite*. The internal grammar is: *I would like this, but asking for it would impose, and I can build a workaround that costs only me*. This is not low self-esteem in the clinical sense; he is not depressive about his worth, he is operationally certain of it. He simply locates his worth in the workaround and not in the wanting. The wanting is something he is willing to carry, alone, indefinitely, as the price of not making it anyone else's logistical problem.

---

## The Core Wound

The wound is **not** the hand. The hand is the scar tissue *over* the wound, and the file makes a category error if it confuses the two.

The core wound is older, structural, and was in place before the first issue: **he was loved, in his family of origin, in proportion to what he absorbed.** Not cruelly, not abusively — there is no canon support for that read, and the household reads as fragile rather than malign. But the conditioning is identical regardless of intent: when a child is the de facto adult by age twelve, the child learns that *the relationship is a load-bearing wall he is holding up*. Remove the load, and the implicit fear — never tested, never falsified, and therefore preserved with perfect freshness into adulthood — is that the wall falls.

From this primary wound, two derivatives follow and structure the rest of the life:

1. **He cannot accept care without converting it into a debt.** Care received is care that must be repaid, ideally with interest, ideally before the giver notices any imbalance. This makes him a poor recipient of friendship, a worse recipient of romance, and an essentially impossible recipient of gratitude. Thank Bruno for something and he will, within the same conversation, find a way to be useful to you again, immediately, so that the books are clear.

2. **He cannot believe that a relationship will survive his unavailability.** Hence the Wakanda transfer (2017), which the file should read not as a developmental opportunity dressed as flight but as a *flight perfectly disguised as a developmental opportunity, including to himself*. He did not leave because he was hurt. He left because he was hurt *and could not figure out how to be in the room while hurt without making the hurt visible*, and visible hurt would be a demand, and demands are impolite. Distance was the only honest expression of the wound that did not require speaking it.

The hand sits on top of all of this. Civil War II handed him, in a single warehouse incident, a literal somatic instantiation of everything that had until then been only structural: he was *right*, Kamala was *wrong*, he paid the bodily cost for her ethical error, and the cost landed precisely on the instrument through which he had organized his entire identity. The wound was already there. The hand made the wound *legible*, and his response to legibility was — diagnostically perfect — to refuse to read it aloud.

---

## How the Wound Is Maintained

The wound persists because every defense Bruno has is also a *virtue*, and the virtues are real, and the social environment rewards the virtues without ever auditing what they cost.

- **Sublimation** routes the longing into the lab; the lab produces results; the results help people; the helping is praised; the praise reinforces the route. Closed loop, indefinitely sustainable, no exit ramp.
- **Altruism-as-defense** means that every time he might have asked for something, he instead gave something, and the giving was received with gratitude, which functioned as proof that the strategy was correct.
- **Intellectualization** means that the few moments at which the wound surfaces are immediately translated into technical vocabulary — *the suit needs a stabilizer*, not *I am terrified you will die* — and the technical vocabulary is then acted upon, which discharges the affect without metabolizing it.
- **Suppression** — the conscious shelving of the hand, the romantic foreclosure, the Kamala-rift — is praised by everyone around him as maturity, because in *episodic* form it *is* maturity. The fact that in Bruno it has become *constitutive* rather than episodic is invisible to observers because the surface presentation is identical.
- **Geographic flight** (Wakanda) is the one primitive defense in his repertoire and the one he is least able to recognize as a defense, because it came packaged with a scholarship and a research program and a new boyfriend. The flight succeeded. The success obscures the flight.
- **Displacement** (the Mike relationship, treated with notable gentleness; the Kareem relationship, treated with notable competence) demonstrates that he can in fact do partnership, *provided the partnership is not pre-loaded with the rescuer-debt structure that the Kamala bond has carried since the first issue*. He is not romantically broken. He is romantically *captured* by one prior commitment that he cannot complete and cannot release.

The maintenance mechanism, summarized: **every time the wound would otherwise surface, his competence intervenes and converts the moment into output**, and the output is valuable, and the valuation reinforces the conversion. He is paid, in the only currency he has trained himself to accept, for not feeling things in public. The bank balance is enormous. There is nothing to spend it on.

---

## The Question the File Cannot Yet Answer

A person whose reliability has never been allowed to fail has not been tested in the only way that would tell us what he is actually made of. The canon, across roughly a decade, has put his body, his romantic life, his geography, and his dominant hand on the table, and he has paid each bill silently. What it has not yet put on the table is **the situation in which there is no one to be useful to** — no Kamala in the next room, no Vick to cover for, no lab to retreat into, no Kareem to be present for, no scholarship to flee toward. Bruno has never been alone with himself for long enough, on the page, for the structure to be stress-tested at the only joint where the file suspects it may be fragile.

The operational hypothesis, which the file flags for any future handler: *Bruno Carrelli's psychological structure is engineered for service and has no idle mode*. Remove the service load entirely and the engine does not stop; it begins to consume itself, quietly, in the same register it has consumed everything else — without complaint, without symptom, without anyone noticing until the noticing comes too late to matter.

---

## Operational Summary

- **Reliability:** Maximal. Has never failed a person he loved and is structurally incapable of beginning now.
- **Discretion:** Maximal. Does not narrate, does not confess, does not leak. The same suppression that costs him personally is, operationally, the most secure communications protocol in the Khan theater.
- **Loyalty:** Absolute, but *non-transferable*. Loyalty is to specific persons, not to causes, institutions, or abstractions. Cannot be recruited; can only be befriended, and befriending him incurs a debt he will pay before you know it exists.
- **Threat-to-mission:** None. He is the stabilizing element in any room he enters.
- **Threat-to-self:** Chronic, sub-clinical, invisible to standard screens. Will not present as crisis. May present, eventually, as a quiet decision — a transfer, a withdrawal, a *getting on with things elsewhere* — that observers will retrospectively recognize as the moment he gave up on something he had never allowed himself to name.
- **Handling note:** Do not thank him. He cannot metabolize gratitude; it converts immediately into renewed obligation. *Ask him what he wants* — directly, repeatedly, in private, with an explicit assurance that the question has no operational consequence. He will not answer the first ten times. The eleventh answer, if it ever comes, is the file's single most valuable possible data point and the only intervention available to anyone who actually wishes him well.
- **Long view:** Bruno Carrelli will be fine. He will be fine the way load-bearing walls are fine: visibly, structurally, and without complaint, right up until they are not. The file's recommendation is that *somebody* — not the apparatus, not a handler, ideally not even a colleague: a friend, in the un-instrumentalized sense — be charged with noticing, on his behalf, what he has trained himself never to notice on his own.

**Bottom line of the bottom line.** He is the steady one. He has been the steady one since he was a child. He will remain the steady one until either someone asks him, in a way he can hear, to put it down for a moment, or until the moment comes when steadiness is no longer something he can produce on demand and the absence of any prior practice at *not* being steady leaves him with no other repertoire. Until then: a young man of unusual seriousness, an engineer of real talent, a friend of unimpeachable quality, and — if the file is honest about what longitudinal observation actually shows — one of the more quietly endangered people in the entire Khan operational field, endangered by no enemy and no power and no plot, but by the success of the architecture he was handed at twelve and has been refining, alone, ever since.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

**Window of coverage:** Birth (c. 1998, by internal dating of *Ms. Marvel* 2014 #1) through approximately age fourteen — i.e., the years preceding his on-page introduction as the Circle Q clerk. This section reconstructs the pre-canonical substrate from the deposits left across Wilson's run (*Ms. Marvel* 2014 #1–19; *Ms. Marvel* 2015 #1–19), the Carrelli-family scenes in the Vick arc (#8–11), Bruno's own narration in #12–13, and the Wakanda-departure issues (2017) where his early biography is most explicitly recounted to Kareem.

---

## 1. Birth, Naming, and the Carrelli Household

**Name.** Bruno Carrelli. The given name is the unselfconscious traditional Italian-Catholic naming convention of a family that has not yet decided to assimilate by surface — there is no "Brian," no anglicized middle name on record. The surname *Carrelli* (from *carrello*, "little cart" — a trade name, the sort that attached to families who worked) places the paternal line within the South Jersey / Hudson County Italian diaspora that has been continuous in Jersey City since the early twentieth century. The texture of the household — the saints' cards visible on the refrigerator in the brief domestic interior of *Ms. Marvel* 2014 #9, the off-hand reference to a grandmother in *Ms. Marvel* 2015 #13 — supports an Italian-American Catholic background that is **cultural rather than devotional**, the moral grammar transmitted without the catechism, the rosary on a hook rather than in a hand.

**Birth and birth order.** Birth dated approximately 1998 (he reads as sixteen in 2014; this is the lower bound — Wilson keeps the Jersey City cohort deliberately tight in age). Older of two children; Vick is the younger by two to three years (he reads as a 13- or 14-year-old freshman during the Inventor arc). No other siblings on record across the entire canon — a fact that itself does work, because it means every gram of household responsibility that was not absorbed by the parents fell on Bruno alone.

**Parental thinness on the page.** The single most diagnostic feature of Bruno's family of origin is the **structural absence of the parents from the narrative frame**. Across nineteen issues of Wilson's 2014 run and nineteen of the 2015 run, Bruno's mother appears in flashback-fragment and reference; his father is named once, glimpsed perhaps once, and otherwise functions as a void at the center of the household. This is not authorial oversight. Wilson populates the Khan household — Yusuf, Muneeba, Aamir, Bruno-as-guest — with persistent specificity. The contrast is the point. **Kamala has a family; Bruno has a job.**

What can be inferred about the parents from the deposits:

- **Mother.** Working, frequently absent on the kind of shift schedule that does not coordinate with school dismissal or dinner. The household-running tasks (Vick's homework supervision, the refrigerator inventory, Vick's truancy notes) default to Bruno rather than to her, which is the signature of a parent stretched thin rather than indifferent. There is no indication of estrangement, addiction, or pathology — only of **insufficiency of presence**, which for a child is its own kind of formative weather.
- **Father.** Even thinner. Bruno does not invoke him in moments where most teenagers would (the Vick crisis; the Wakanda decision; the injury). The silence is uniform enough to suggest either physical absence, emotional unavailability of long standing, or both. There is no canon of paternal abuse — Bruno carries none of the somatic signatures (flinch response, hyper-attunement to male tone) that would indicate it. The likeliest reconstruction is a father present in the building but not in the role: working long, tired, ceding the field.

**Household finances.** Fragile, sub-precarious-but-not-catastrophic. Bruno has been working a paid shift at the Circle Q since middle school (his own line, *Ms. Marvel* 2014 #1), which is illegal under New Jersey labor law before age fourteen and irregular until sixteen — the implication is that Mr. Khan (Bruno's employer at the Circle Q, who is *not* Kamala's father — different Khan; the Circle Q owner) cut the kid an off-the-books arrangement because the kid needed it and was visibly reliable. A family that lets a twelve-year-old take an off-books shift at a convenience store is a family in which the marginal twenty dollars matters.

---

## 2. The Sibling Substrate: Vick, and the Manufacture of a Parentified Child

The single most consequential relationship of Bruno's childhood is his relationship to Vick. Every other formative pattern routes through it.

**Vick's temperament.** Across the Inventor arc (*Ms. Marvel* 2014 #8–11) and his later returns, Vick is canonically the **chaotic-impulsive** sibling — easily flattered, easily recruited, attracted to whoever offers him status quickly. He drops out of structured paths, gets into the wrong rooms, takes the wrong jobs. None of this reads as malice; Vick is not a bad kid. He is a kid whose nervous system is differently calibrated than his brother's, and who in a properly-resourced family would have been caught early and held. He was not caught early. He was caught by Bruno, repeatedly, after he had already fallen.

**The role-reversal mechanism.** By the time Bruno is twelve, he is doing three jobs the household needs and is structurally incapable of allocating:

1. **Earning** (the Circle Q shifts).
2. **Surveilling Vick** (knowing where he is, whom he is with, what he is into — the older-sibling-as-parole-officer function visible in #8–9).
3. **Absorbing the shame Vick generates** so that it does not reach the parents in a form that would either crush them further or escalate into household conflict.

The third is the most psychologically expensive and the most diagnostic. Bruno does not report Vick's troubles upward; he metabolizes them laterally. When Vick falls in with the Inventor's child-labor cell (#8), Bruno's instinct — *concealment, self-handled rescue, only reluctantly bringing Kamala in when the problem outstrips him* — is not improvised in 2014. It is the practiced motor pattern of a child who has been managing his brother's failures privately for years, because the household structure had no other shock-absorber.

**Earliest behavioral pattern, fully formed by age twelve:** **absorb privately, ask only when forced, never present the bill.** This will recur in every domain of his life and is the master pattern from which everything else in §§3–5 of the workup descends.

---

## 3. The Catholic Substrate

Bruno's Catholicism is *atmospheric* rather than practiced. He is never depicted at Mass; he does not cross himself; he does not invoke saints. What he carries from the cultural inheritance is the **moral architecture**: a deontological reflex (the right thing is the harder thing, owed regardless of outcome), a quiet asceticism around self-indulgence (no drinking, no partying, no boasting), a familiarity with **suffering-as-meaningful** that allows him to absorb the hand injury later without melodrama, and a quasi-confessional discomfort with leaving wrongs un-named even when naming them costs him (he tells Kamala she is wrong about Ulysses; the Catholic boy cannot let the friend walk into the error unwarned).

What he does **not** carry: the metaphysics, the eschatology, the institutional loyalty. The substrate furnishes him with conscience without furnishing him with consolation — which means that when the costs accrue, he has no theology to absorb them and no confessor to hand them to. They go into the body and into the workbench.

---

## 4. Jersey City as Formative Environment

The geography matters as much as the family. Bruno is a **Jersey City native of the waterfront cohort** — a working-class urban kid raised within walking distance of the Circle Q, the Khans' block, the boardwalk, the school. The city in his childhood is the post-2008 Jersey City: still pre-gentrification at the neighborhood-Greenville/Bergen-Lafayette grain, with the Newport towers visible across the skyline as the *other* city Bruno is not part of. The Circle Q itself — the corner store, the night clerk, the bell on the door — is the **central node** of his geography from before adolescence: not just a workplace but the room in which he first learned to read adults, calm strangers, calculate change under fluorescent light, and remain unflustered while someone else's chaos walked through the door. Half of the somatic equipment he brings to the Kamala partnership later — the unflappability, the *Are you okay?* reflex, the instinctive de-escalation — was trained on the Circle Q counter by age thirteen.

**Schooling.** Coles Academic High School (introduced as Kamala's school, where Bruno is a classmate from at least middle school onward). Bruno is the kid who *should* have been tracked into the magnet/STEM channel earlier than he was and likely was not, because the household never had the bandwidth to file the paperwork, attend the parent nights, or push back when the teacher under-recommended him. His scientific seriousness in canon is **autodidactic in origin** — the lab competence visible from *Ms. Marvel* 2014 #3 onward is too sophisticated to be school-issued and reads as the product of a child who taught himself electronics from manuals, YouTube, and salvage, in back rooms, after shifts.

**Friendship density.** Sparse. Bruno enters the 2014 canon with essentially **one** real friendship — Kamala — and a polite acquaintance-set otherwise. This is not the profile of a child who failed at making friends; it is the profile of a child who *did not have the hours*. A boy who works the after-school shift, supervises his brother, and self-teaches engineering has no Saturday afternoons to spend. The narrow friendship surface he presents at sixteen is the natural output of a childhood in which discretionary social time was the first resource sacrificed.

---

## 5. The Kamala Bond: Origin and Pre-History

The Bruno–Kamala friendship predates the canon by years. By the timeline implicit in their interactions in *Ms. Marvel* 2014 #1–3 — the easy shorthand, the standing presence at the Khan dinner table referenced retrospectively, the fact that Muneeba Khan knows and trusts Bruno on sight — they have been close since middle school, plausibly since fifth or sixth grade.

The **founding asymmetry** is established in this pre-canon period and never recalibrates. Kamala is the imaginative, family-anchored, slightly-overprotected daughter of a stable household; Bruno is the under-anchored boy who has been functionally adult since before puberty. From the start, the relational gradient runs one direction: **Bruno stabilizes Kamala; Kamala animates Bruno.** She is the room he was let into where the air was warmer than at home. He is the bench she could put her weight on without thinking. Neither child is conscious of the asymmetry — Kamala because she is twelve and her household has always been warm, Bruno because the asymmetry is the only configuration he has ever known a relationship to take.

The **romantic vector** dates almost certainly from this pre-canonical period as well. Bruno does not "develop" feelings for Kamala in 2014; he arrives in panel one already carrying them. The longitudinal evidence supports a crush of multi-year standing, formed in the window where she went from playmate to person and he had no other intimate field in which to deposit the awakening of adolescent attachment. That she was the only girl in his close orbit — and that the closeness was already total before the feelings arrived — locked the pattern in early: the love is **structurally indistinguishable, in his nervous system, from the friendship**, which is part of why he cannot extract one without endangering the other, and part of why, years later, the confession in Civil War II detonates rather than lands.

---

## 6. Formative Traumas (Sub-Acute, Cumulative)

Bruno's childhood contains **no single catastrophic trauma** of the kind that would be flagged in a standard intake. There is no death, no abuse, no displacement, no documented neglect. What there is, instead, is the **slow accretion of micro-stressors** characteristic of the parentified child:

- **The recurring crisis of Vick** — every truancy, every disappearance, every wrong friend, metabolized privately and absorbed into Bruno's nervous system as baseline vigilance.
- **The repeated experience of needing a parent and finding the room empty** — not dramatically, just *routinely*, until the expectation re-shaped itself and the need stopped being formulated.
- **Financial micro-stress** — the kind that does not produce eviction but produces a child who learns, by age ten, to read a register tape and to feel a household's monthly cash position in his stomach.
- **The structural loneliness of being the competent one in a room of people who are not.** Bruno was, almost certainly, the smartest person in his household from age eight onward. This is a specific kind of childhood injury — being the one who has to translate the world to the adults around you, who can never be carried because you are already carrying.

Cumulatively these constitute what would be called, in a more clinical register, **chronic developmental over-responsibility** — the absence of catastrophe in the presence of unrelenting low-grade demand. The body adapts. The personality calcifies around the adaptation. By thirteen, Bruno *is* the adaptation: the quiet boy at the counter who notices everything, says little, fixes what he can, and does not present the bill.

---

## 7. Earliest Behavioral Patterns — The Templates Already Set by Age Fourteen

By the eve of the canon, the following patterns are fully established and will not change in their fundamentals across the next decade of story:

1. **De-escalation reflex.** Walking into the Circle Q confrontation in #1 and lowering the temperature without raising his voice — this is not a sixteen-year-old's invention; it is the trained reflex of a kid who has been defusing his household and his customers since middle school.
2. **Risk-assessment-on-behalf-of-another.** The *Are you okay?* response to Kamala's first transformation (#3) is a Vick-trained motor pattern transposed onto a new object.
3. **Concealment of own cost.** Visible in the Vick rescue arc, but already canonical in his approach to his own work hours, his own fatigue, his own academic load. He does not narrate strain.
4. **Sublimation into the bench.** The lab as the room where the unspeakable becomes the solderable. Established before the canon opens; intensifies under every subsequent stressor.
5. **Romantic deferral.** The pre-canon multi-year unspoken crush is the prototype of every later romantic decision — the bid held back, the alternative (Mike, later Kareem) sought in the orbit rather than the center.
6. **Geographic stability as a value, eventually as a defense.** Bruno's pre-canon world is small and walkable — Circle Q, school, home, Khan apartment. He has never left it. This will make the Wakanda transfer, when it comes, legible as the magnitude of rupture it actually is: the boy who built his nervous system on a six-block radius will put an ocean and a continent between himself and the wound, because the smaller distances no longer suffice.

---

**Section summary.** Bruno Carrelli enters the canon at sixteen as a person who has, in effect, already lived an adult life for four years. The childhood is not lurid; it is the quieter and more common American formative environment of the **competent eldest in a thinly-staffed working-class household** — Italian-Catholic in moral grammar, Jersey City in geography, Circle Q in vocational nursery, Vick in training-load, Kamala in emotional center of gravity. There is no founding wound. There is a founding *configuration*, and the configuration is the wound: a child given a load he was temperamentally equipped to carry, in a family that did not have the capacity to notice he was carrying it, in a city that rewarded the carrying with a paycheck and a counter to stand behind. Everything subsequent in the file — the lab, the love, the silence, the hand, the exile — is built on this floor.


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

**File reference:** UATU/BC-02/FORM-EMRG
**Window of record:** Approximately age 11 (middle-school employment onset, ~2010 by Wilson-era internal chronology) through age 17–18 (post–Civil War II disposition; Wakanda relocation, 2017). Supplementary observation through the Ahmed transition (2019) where it bears on identity-set.
**Operational thesis of this section:** Bruno Carrelli does not have an "emergence" in the metahuman sense. His emergence is the slow visible accretion of a *function* — the boy who fixes — into an *identity* — the one who is reliably there — and then the public, witnessed *cost* of that identity, sustained in his dominant hand on a warehouse floor in Jersey City at sixteen. Every later behavior referenced in this dossier traces to the formation arc mapped here.

---

## I. Pre-Subject Substrate: The Carrelli Household, Approximate Period Age 0–11

The Carrelli family unit, as reconstructed from longitudinal incidental evidence (Wilson, *Ms. Marvel* 2014 #1–19; *Ms. Marvel* 2015 #1–19; passing references in Ahmed/Saladin), is a working-class Italian-American Catholic household on the Jersey City waterfront, occupying a rental footprint within walking distance of the Circle Q convenience store on Westside Avenue. Mother: present, working, recurrently absent across multiple shifts; father: minimally on-page, contextual evidence suggests episodic presence at best, no scenes of paternal instruction or discipline involving Bruno are on record. Surveillance reading: not a one-parent household by legal definition, but functionally one-and-a-quarter, with the quarter unpredictable.

Younger brother **Vick Carrelli** (approx. 2–3 years junior) is in the home from Bruno's earliest ages of memory. The asymmetry between the brothers — Bruno organized, Vick impulsive — is presented as longstanding; nothing in the record suggests a clean precipitating event for Vick's later delinquency. The most economical reading is **chronic temperamental difference compounded by chronic supervisory thinness**: Vick was the kid who needed more attention than the household structure produced, and Bruno was the kid in the next bedroom.

**Inferred granular pattern, ages ~7–11:**
- Bruno is the one who knows where the keys are.
- Bruno is the one who knows what time Vick was supposed to be home.
- Bruno is the one who calls when the milk runs out.
- Bruno does homework at the kitchen table with one ear on the door.
- Bruno learns to cook eggs, pasta, sandwich-tier dinners well before peer baseline.
- Bruno's tolerance for noise is high; his tolerance for *unaccountability* is the variable that calcifies into character.

There is no recorded trauma — no death, no abuse, no instability of the kind that demands a CPS file. The formative pressure on Bruno is **subtractive, not additive**: not what happened to him but what failed to happen *for* him. He was not damaged. He was *load-bearing earlier than the design specifications called for.*

---

## II. The Circle Q Onset, Approximately Age 11–13

The single most consequential biographical fact of Bruno Carrelli's adolescence is that **he begins working at the Circle Q convenience store in middle school**, well before legal employment age, in a configuration that the record presents as informal-permissive (the store's owner, Mr. Blevin, tolerates and eventually formalizes the arrangement). Wilson establishes by *Ms. Marvel* 2014 #1 that by age 16 Bruno's presence behind the counter is so naturalized that customers — Kamala included — treat him as a fixture of the building rather than an employee with a schedule.

**Behavioral pattern, micro-grain:**
- Bruno's first earned dollars enter the Carrelli household rather than a savings account.
- He learns to count change before he learns to drive.
- He learns customer-deescalation — the specific tonal flattening required to defuse the angry adult buying lottery tickets, the specific cheerful neutrality required for the regular who tips in pennies — before he learns to flirt.
- He learns the rhythms of a building that other people pass through and he does not: opens, closes, restock, the back room.
- The **back room of the Circle Q** becomes, by age 13–14, his **first laboratory**. Soldering iron, salvaged parts, schematic notebooks. This is operationally critical: his scientific vocation does not begin in a school program. It begins in *unsupervised time on the clock at a job he should not legally have*, which means his identity as a maker is fused, at the cellular level, with his identity as a worker, which is fused with his identity as the one who is providing.

The Circle Q is therefore not a workplace in Bruno's mental geography. It is **the room where he is allowed to be capable**. Home is the room where he is required to be capable. School is the room where his capability is graded. The Circle Q back room is the only one where capability and pleasure coincide. This distinction explains the entire later pattern of his preferring solitary night work to social hours; it is not introversion, it is *the only inherited geography in which being good at something has never been weaponized as a demand.*

---

## III. Coregan Middle / Coles Academic — School-Era Identity, Approximately Age 12–15

The school record is sparse on-page but reconstructable from peer placement. Bruno attends the same Jersey City school system as Kamala Khan, Nakia Bahadir, Zoe Zimmer, and Josh Richardson; by high school all are at Coles Academic. Inferred academic profile: high-achieving in math and physical sciences, undistinguished-to-quiet in English and social studies, perfect attendance, never on a detention list, never on an honors-assembly stage either. **He is the student teachers remember as "a good kid" and cannot quote a single specific thing he said in class.** This is consistent with the parentified-child pattern of *visible reliability without performative self-display*.

**Friendship sociometry, age ~12 onward:**
- **Kamala Khan.** First documented interaction predates *Ms. Marvel* 2014 #1 by years. The friendship is established by the pilot issue as *baseline*, with the in-joke fluency that takes a half-decade of low-grade daily contact to develop. Bruno is, from the start, the friend who *waits* — at the counter, at the locker, at the corner — for Kamala to arrive. Pattern set early: he is the stable coordinate; she moves through.
- **Nakia Bahadir.** Stable peripheral friendship via Kamala. Bruno reads Nakia accurately and early; treats her seriously when others (Zoe) condescend. No romantic vector.
- **Zoe Zimmer.** Tolerated rather than befriended. Bruno's tonal handling of Zoe in *Ms. Marvel* 2014 #1 — polite, non-combative, faintly distancing — is a microcosm of his general handling of social actors he reads as performing rather than present.
- **Mike (Michaela Miller).** Will enter the field later (age ~15–16). Pre-relationship period: Bruno is known to her as Kamala's friend.

**Crucially absent from the school-era record:** Bruno is not in clubs. Not on teams. Not in the band. Not in student government. His extracurricular life *is the Circle Q and the back-room lab*. He is the child who, when surveyed about hobbies, would say "I work," and the surveyor would not register this as a developmental flag because the work is voluntary in appearance.

---

## IV. The Pre-Emergence Crush, Approximately Age 14–16

By Wilson's account the romantic substrate is established before Kamala's Terrigenesis. Bruno is in love with Kamala for at least one full year, plausibly two, before *Ms. Marvel* 2014 #1. The interior evidence is the *fluency* of his attention in the pilot — he knows what she will and will not eat, what she is and is not allowed to do, which of her brother's moods to ask about, which to skip. This is not new attention. This is *practiced* attention.

**Micro-pattern, granular:**
- He looks up when the bell over the Circle Q door rings. He does not look up for every customer. He looks up for her.
- He stocks the things she likes at eye-level. (Inferred from layout-consistency across early issues.)
- He has rehearsed, internally, several versions of the sentence "I like you" and discarded all of them on the same grounds: *it would make her uncomfortable, and I am the one she comes to when she is uncomfortable, and I cannot be both the source of and the relief from her discomfort.* This is not stated on-page. It is the only internal logic that fits the external behavior.

The decision **not to speak** is therefore made — provisionally, renewably — *before the operational period of this dossier begins*. Bruno's adolescence is the period in which he learns that his desire is *structurally incompatible* with his function, and that the function is more important to him than the desire. This is the foundational suppression. Every later one is a copy of this one.

---

## V. Terrigenesis Night and Disclosure (*Ms. Marvel* 2014 #1–3) — Age 16

The Terrigen Mist event over Jersey City is the *external* emergence of the Kamala-as-Ms.-Marvel system. It is **also**, with equal importance, the emergence of *Bruno-as-infrastructure*. The two are coextensive. There is no Ms. Marvel without the boy behind the counter.

**Surveillance reconstruction of the disclosure sequence (#3):**

- Kamala, mid-transformation and mid-crisis, comes to the Circle Q because *that is where Bruno is*. Note: she does not go home. She does not go to Nakia. She goes to the building where the reliable person is reliably located. **Bruno's geographic constancy is already, by age 16, a community resource.**
- Bruno sees her *before* she chooses to disclose. The disclosure is therefore not a gift she gives him; it is a fact she cannot prevent him from observing. This matters: his subsequent loyalty is not transactional ("you trusted me, I'll keep faith") but **constitutional** ("I saw, and now I am responsible for what I saw"). The Catholic moral grammar — witness implies obligation — is operative here even though Bruno's active religious practice is residual.
- His first verbalized response is operational: **"Are you okay?"** Not "what are you," not "show me again," not "this is amazing." The clause is diagnostic. *He is checking for damage before he is processing wonder.* This is the parentified child's reflex applied to a metahuman incident.
- Within hours — by the next issue — he is **prototyping**. The polymer-stabilizer for her costume, the early diagnostic work on her embiggening biology, the cataloguing of her observed limits. He has converted shock into engineering inside a single news cycle. This is sublimation working at peak efficiency, and it is also self-protection: as long as he is *building*, he is not *reacting*, and reaction is the affective register he has not been trained for.

**Identity-formation note:** This is the moment Bruno's life acquires a *vocation* in the Weberian sense — a calling whose service organizes the rest of the days. Before the disclosure he was a smart kid with a job and a crush. After the disclosure he is **the person who keeps the secret, builds the equipment, names the risks, and waits at the agreed-upon corner.** The role is total. He accepts it within minutes. He never renegotiates the terms.

---

## VI. The Inventor Arc and the Vick Crisis (*Ms. Marvel* 2014 #8–11) — Age 16

The first full-pressure stress test of the formed identity arrives within months of disclosure. Vick Carrelli, by now ~13–14, has fallen into the Inventor's child-labor cell. Surveillance reconstruction of Bruno's behavior in this arc is the cleanest available document of his core pattern under load:

1. **He learns of Vick's situation and does not tell Kamala.** First instinct: contain it inside the family. Family shame is private. The Carrelli structural fragility is *his* secret to keep, not the community's emergency to absorb.
2. **He attempts to retrieve Vick himself.** Unarmed, untrained, sixteen years old, against organized adversary. The risk calculus is not "can I succeed" but "can I avoid involving anyone else." The decision is *not heroic*. It is *parental.* It is what an exhausted single parent would do at 2 a.m. when the school has called for the third time.
3. **He nearly dies.** This is not narrated as fear. It is narrated as *what happened next*. The affective flatness around his own near-death is the earliest clear marker of the affect-containment pattern that will define his entire later presentation.
4. **Only when contained-solution fails does he involve Kamala.** And when he does, the request is framed as *Vick's* emergency, not Bruno's. He never asks her to come because *he* is afraid. He asks her to come because *Vick* is in danger. The grammatical sleight is the entire personality in one sentence.
5. **He does not extract gratitude.** Post-rescue, there is no scene of reckoning, no "you almost died for my brother." The cost is absorbed and not invoiced.

**Operational read:** Vick is the *training ground* for Bruno's relationship to Kamala. Every behavior he will later display toward Kamala under threat — silent absorption of risk, refusal to invoice, containment-then-escalation-only-under-failure, framing his fear as someone else's emergency — is rehearsed first on his brother. The Kamala-pattern is the Vick-pattern with a different name on the door.

---

## VII. Mike Miller — The Displacement Relationship, Approximately Age 16–17

The Mike Miller relationship enters the operational record after the Inventor arc and runs through and past Civil War II. It is **the single most ethically delicate datum in the formation period**, because the easy reading — Bruno is using Mike as a substitute — is partially true and not the whole truth.

**Surveillance-grade granularity:**
- Mike is genuinely kind. Bruno is genuinely fond. The relationship is not cynical.
- *And:* the relationship begins in the temporal window when Kamala's heroic and romantic life has expanded past Bruno's gravitational reach, and it is structured around Mike's apparent willingness to ask nothing destabilizing of him. Mike is the relationship in which Bruno **does not have to be the one who builds things**. Mike does not need a stabilizer for her costume. Mike does not need a ride to a warehouse. Mike's emotional bid on him is *peer-coded*, not *infrastructure-coded*, and this is, for a parentified child, both novel and disorienting.
- He treats Mike with respect, with attention, with what reads as real tenderness — *and* he does not give her the part of himself that is reserved for the longing he will not speak. The relationship is therefore complete on Mike's terms and incomplete on Bruno's, and Mike (perceptive) eventually clocks this. The arc ends without rancor and without restoration. Bruno does not learn from the Mike relationship that he was wrong to displace; he learns that *displacement, even gentle displacement, is visible to a perceptive partner.* This will shape every later partnership.

The Mike relationship is, in the formation arc, the **first** field-test of Bruno's capacity to receive care he has not earned through service. He does not pass it. He does not fail it loudly. He passes it on a curve.

---

## VIII. The Ulysses Crisis — Pre-Injury Ethical Position (Civil War II tie-ins, *Ms. Marvel* 2015 #7–11) — Age 16–17

Before the warehouse, before the hand, Bruno's role in the predictive-profiling controversy is **the role of the person who saw it first**. He names the Ulysses problem — that acting on probabilistic foresight against not-yet-perpetrators is a categorical wrong, not a difficult tradeoff — before Kamala does, and he names it on **deontological grounds**: people have not done a thing until they have done it, and to treat them as having done it is to abolish the moral status of choice.

The granularity of this matters. Bruno does not argue from outcomes ("this will go badly"). He argues from rights ("this is not ours to do"). The flavor is *Catholic-philosophical-residual* — the moral grammar of a kid who grew up around a faith he no longer practices but whose ethical syntax he never replaced. He is, at sixteen-seventeen, **the most ethically articulate person in Kamala's social field**, and Kamala, under institutional pressure (Captain Marvel, the Avengers infrastructure, the New Jersey deputy-program), does not listen.

**Formative significance:** This is the first time being right has not been enough. Through Vick, through the Inventor, through the early hero work, Bruno's correctness has tracked with Bruno's usefulness — he was right *and* he was the one she went to. In the Ulysses arc he is right *and she goes past him*. The relational geometry shifts. He is no longer in the loop; he is the *obstacle to her current loop*. This is the precondition of the warehouse.

---

## IX. The Warehouse — Civil War II Inflection (*Ms. Marvel* 2015 #12) — Age 17

Operationally this is the single event in Bruno Carrelli's formation that the entire later record points back to. Surveillance reconstruction below is granular because the granularity is the point.

**The decision to go.** Bruno goes to the warehouse not to *fight* but to *prevent* — to physically interpose between Kamala and the action he believes will cost her the moral self he loves. He goes alone. He does not warn Aamir, Nakia, anyone. *Containment within the family of choice*, same pattern as the Vick rescue. He does not bring a weapon. He brings himself.

**The mechanism of injury.** Crush/blast trauma to the right (dominant) hand during the confrontation. The injury is sustained while Bruno is positioned between Kamala's intended target and Kamala. The hand is, with brutal narrative economy, the part of him that built her equipment — and it is the part that is destroyed in the act of trying to stop her from misusing the moral architecture he helped build. **The body part and the role are the same object.** The injury is therefore not metaphor decorating event; it is event achieving the structural lucidity of metaphor.

**Behavioral pattern on the floor and after:**
- Bruno does not scream at Kamala.
- Bruno does not, in any subsequent scene, say "you did this."
- Bruno does not name the injury as her fault in any internal monologue accessible to the record.
- Bruno does not refuse to see her.
- Bruno does *withdraw*. He becomes quieter. He becomes more contained. The verbal-affective bandwidth of their friendship collapses by approximately one order of magnitude inside two weeks of recovery.
- He resumes lab work within days. **One-handed.** This is the parentified child's reflex applied to his own damaged body: do not stop, do not center the wound, find the workaround, ship the next deliverable.

**The thing he does not do, and which the file flags as diagnostic of the entire personality:** he never asks her to apologize. Not because she should not — she should — but because **the apology would require him to occupy the position of the wounded party**, and that position is not in his self-concept's vocabulary. He cannot be the one who needs Kamala's repair. The relationship's geometry does not permit it. So the wound is metabolized in silence, and the silence becomes the new shape of the friendship.

---

## X. The Wakanda Decision — Geographic Solution to a Relational Problem (*Ms. Marvel* 2015 #13–19; Wilson's late run, 2017) — Age 17–18

The transfer to the Wakandan science academy is presented in canon as **opportunity**: a scholarship, a developmental ascent, an unambiguous good. The surveillance read does not contest the opportunity. It contests the *primacy* of the opportunity as causal.

The decision-tree, reconstructed:
- *Stay in Jersey City and continue as Kamala's infrastructure with a damaged hand:* untenable. The somatic basis of his role is compromised; remaining in the role while degraded would force a daily reckoning he cannot stage.
- *Stay in Jersey City and step back from the role:* untenable. There is no version of being near Kamala in which he is not pulled into the role. The role is geographic as much as relational; the Circle Q is on her route.
- *Stay in Jersey City and confess, renegotiate, repair:* **the option he does not consider on-page.** This is the diagnostic absence. The confrontational repair-path is not in his decision space at all. The personality has no firmware for it.
- *Leave.* Distance as solution. Wakanda is opportunity-coded, which makes it *say-able*. He cannot say "I have to get away from her." He can say "I have to take this scholarship." The opportunity is real; the *deployment* of the opportunity is a flight.

**This is the first time Bruno solves a relational problem by removing his body from the field.** Up to this point his entire pattern has been *stay and absorb*. The Wakanda transfer is a pattern-break: *leave and reset*. It works — he stabilizes, he does new work, he forms the Kareem relationship — but it sets a precedent. The next time the field becomes unbearable, the body will know that the door is an option. This is, in the operational long view, the **single most consequential behavioral acquisition of his entire formation arc**, and it is acquired at age seventeen.

---

## XI. Kareem and the Reconstitution Period (late Wilson, into Ahmed) — Age 17–18+

The Kareem (Red Dagger) relationship begins in the post-injury, partially post-exile period. Surveillance read:

- Kareem is **in Kamala's orbit but not Kamala**. Bruno's romantic life continues to organize itself around the *gravitational neighborhood* of his primary attachment, which is itself diagnostic — he has not learned, in the formation period, to want outside the orbit. He has only learned to want adjacent to it.
- Kareem is **competent, self-possessed, and not in need of infrastructure**. The relationship is therefore the first in Bruno's life in which his partner is *operationally peer or superior*, and Bruno's value to the partner is not his usefulness. This is corrective. It is not curative. Patterns of self-erasure are softened in the Kareem partnership but not abolished.
- The relationship's *international* geometry — distance, intermittence — happens to suit Bruno's newly acquired comfort with absence-as-management. He chose, structurally, a relationship in which the *capacity to leave* is built into the architecture. The body has learned, and is now organizing around what it learned.

---

## XII. The Steady-State Emergence — End of Formation, ~Age 18

By the close of the formation arc — and the handoff to the Ahmed/Saladin operational period covered in the next dossier section — Bruno Carrelli has settled into the configuration that will define him for the entire remainder of the longitudinal record:

- **Vocation:** scientist/engineer, working at a level that makes him peer-functional with Wakandan academy talent, the Stark/Pym infrastructure, and eventually the X-adjacent technical layer.
- **Role:** *steady professional*. No longer Kamala's infrastructure-primary; instead, the adult-coded technical and ethical presence in any room he enters, including rooms containing literal superhuman elders.
- **Body:** permanently altered. The right hand is a load-bearing limitation he has routed around, never around in a


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# CHRONOLOGY III — THE DEFINING MIDDLE PERIOD

**Scope:** Roughly *Ms. Marvel* (2014) #8 through the close of the Wilson run and the threshold of Ahmed's *Magnificent Ms. Marvel* (≈2015–2019 publication; in-universe a compressed adolescence of perhaps two to three years). This is the period in which Bruno Carrelli ceases to be a supporting fixture and becomes a load-bearing column — and then the period in which that column visibly cracks, is patched, and is relocated.

---

## I. THE INVENTOR ARC AND THE VICK CRISIS *(Ms. Marvel 2014 #8–11)*

The middle period opens not with a fight but with a phone call Bruno does not make. Vick Carrelli — younger brother, chronic disappointment, the household's permanent open wound — has fallen in with the Inventor's child-labor cell, and Bruno discovers it before anyone else does. His first instinct is the diagnostic one of his whole life: **conceal, triage, fix in private.** He does not tell Aamir. He does not tell his parents (who, per the canon's pointed silences, are not the kind of parents to whom a Carrelli boy *tells* things). He does not, initially, tell Kamala.

The pattern in those few panels is the entire pattern of his middle period in miniature:

1. **Latency** — a beat in which he tries to absorb the problem alone.
2. **Recruitment-as-last-resort** — bringing Kamala in only when the problem exceeds his unaided capacity, and framing the ask as small even when it is large.
3. **Bodily forward-deployment** — putting himself between the danger and the people he loves, on the unspoken theory that his body is the most acceptable expendable in the room.
4. **No accounting afterward** — refusing to convert the cost into a debt.

He is nearly killed in the rescue. Alphona draws him sweat-soaked, scraped, the goggles cocked, the shoulders hunched in the specific posture of a teenager pretending the adrenaline is fine. Kamala thanks him. He deflects. Vick is recovered. The Carrelli family does not, in any depicted scene, sit down and talk about what happened. Bruno files it.

**Behavioral residue (post-Vick):**
- He begins double-shifting at Circle Q with new consistency — partly Vick's legal fees, partly the Carrelli household's perennial thinness, partly because the back room is where his lab is and the lab is where he is least required to *be a person*.
- He starts locking the back-room door from the inside. (Minor; visible in two background panels across the run; consistent.)
- He stops mentioning his parents at all. Across the remainder of Wilson, parental references collapse to near-zero. Vick is referenced; the parents are scenery.

---

## II. THE GADGET YEARS — BRUNO AS INFRASTRUCTURE *(Ms. Marvel 2014 #12–19; 2015 #1–5)*

This is the long quiet stretch in which Bruno *builds*. The narrative foregrounds Kamala; the substrate foregrounds him. Every Ms. Marvel costume iteration in this window passes through his hands. The polymer stress-tolerance of the fabric (it has to stretch when she embiggens), the comm earpiece, the inhibitor calibrations against Inhuman bio-signatures, the Lockjaw-summoning device, the bespoke modifications after each new villain teaches them a new failure mode — all his work, almost all of it done after midnight, almost all of it done one-handed-by-preference even when both hands still worked, because he liked the discipline of it.

**Operational tempo in this period (reconstructed from on-page evidence + reasonable inference):**

- **Circle Q shift:** afternoons into early evening, school days; full days on weekends.
- **Lab work:** 22:00 to 02:00 nightly, with longer pushes after every Ms. Marvel incident. He sleeps approximately five hours on a school night, four after a mission.
- **Homework:** done in fifteen-minute bursts between customers at the register; he is consistently A/A- without effort the canon ever shows him expending, which means the effort is invisible because it has been routinized into the gaps.
- **Caloric pattern:** Circle Q inventory (pre-wrapped sandwiches, energy bars, sodas) eaten at the counter; rarely a sit-down meal except at the Khans'. Muneeba Khan feeds him without comment on multiple occasions; she has noticed.
- **Phone behavior:** answers Kamala on the first ring, every time, including during shifts and during sleep. Answers Vick in two or three. Answers Aamir politely. Answers his parents — when they call, which is seldom — flatly.

**The Mike relationship begins** in this stretch (Michaela Miller, introduced in this window). It is a real relationship and the canon refuses to make it cynical. Mike is funny, perceptive, generous; Bruno is genuinely fond of her; they have a tactile, easy warmth that he does not have with Kamala because with Kamala every touch is freighted. The displacement reading is correct but partial — Mike is also, on her own terms, *good for him*, and he knows it, and he tries. The failure mode is not that he treats her badly. The failure mode is that he never tells Kamala about her until Kamala finds out, and the *not-telling* is its own confession, and Mike eventually reads it.

**Pattern entrenched in this period:**
- He becomes the person other people's parents trust. Yusuf Khan greets him by first name and by hand on shoulder. Sheikh Abdullah nods to him on the street. Zoe's mother (briefly, off-page) refers to him as "the polite one." He has, by sixteen, accumulated the social capital of a man twice his age, and he has spent none of it on himself.
- He develops a fixed circuit: home → Circle Q → Khan house (back door, never front) → school → Circle Q → home. Deviations from this circuit in this period are rare enough to be diagnostically significant when they occur.
- He stops going to parties entirely. (He was never a frequent attendee; in this stretch attendance drops to zero.)

---

## III. THE LAST EASY MONTHS *(late Ms. Marvel 2015 #1–11)*

There is a window — short, retrospectively luminous — in which Bruno and Kamala operate as a functional partnership and both of them seem, briefly, *happy* in the ordinary sense. Loki shows up at the school dance and Bruno is wry about it. Kamarias and embarrassments compound; he metabolizes them with humor. He teaches her, in passing, to solder. She breaks his soldering iron. He buys another and does not mention it.

This is the period in which his pre-injury baseline is most legible, and it matters because the contrast after the injury is the measure of the loss.

**Pre-injury baseline (catalogued for diagnostic comparison):**
- **Hands:** in constant low-grade motion. Tapping the counter in 4/4. Rotating a pen through the fingers (right-handed default, ambidextrous capable). Folding receipt paper into geometric shapes left at the register for the next shift.
- **Speech:** quick, dry, full sentences, low volume, frequent self-interruption to revise for precision.
- **Eye contact:** steady with Kamala, intermittent with everyone else.
- **Smile:** asymmetrical, left side first, slow to commit; a full smile requires Kamala in the room.
- **Posture at workbench:** leaned forward, both elbows on the surface, chin tucked, brow knit, an absorbed stillness broken only by the hands.

This baseline is about to be permanently disrupted, and a complete-surveillance file marks the boundary precisely because everything after will be measured against it.

---

## IV. THE ULYSSES PROBLEM AND THE PROFILING DISPUTE *(Civil War II tie-ins, Ms. Marvel 2015 #7–11)*

Bruno reads the Ulysses problem before Kamala does. This is documented. He names it in technical-ethical register — *predictive output is not evidence, it is a probability distribution, and a probability distribution is not a warrant* — when Kamala is still riding the operational high of having a tool that seems to make her job easier. The disagreement is the first sustained ethical rupture between them, and it follows the script of every important Bruno conversation: he says the harder thing once, clearly, in measured language; he does not repeat it; he does not escalate; he watches her choose the other path and he stays.

**Key behavioral marker:** in the panels where Kamala defends the profiling program, Bruno's hands go still. This is the single most reliable distress-tell in his repertoire and it appears in roughly five distinct incidents across the run. The hands stop. The face does not change. The body does not lean away. Only the hands.

He keeps building her gear. He keeps showing up. He keeps, in private — at the workbench, at 01:00, alone — running the numbers on the predictive program's false-positive rate and not telling her he is doing it.

---

## V. THE WAREHOUSE — THE HAND *(Ms. Marvel 2015 #12; CW:II crossover, 2016)*

The injury itself takes a single page. The middle period pivots on it.

**Mechanism (as depicted):** explosion-adjacent crush/blast in the warehouse confrontation; right hand caught between mass and detonation; nerve damage, soft-tissue damage, loss of fine motor control. He is conscious throughout. He does not scream. He says Kamala's name once, in a register the colorist renders dim.

**The first 72 hours (reconstructed from on-page sequence and reasonable inference):**

- **Hour 0–4:** ER, Jersey City Medical Center. Mother arrives. Father is "on his way." Vick arrives before the father does. Kamala arrives in civvies and does not let go of his good hand.
- **Hour 4–24:** initial surgery; sedation; first conversations with the hand specialist conducted while Bruno is too anesthetized to perform the composure he will perform from this point forward.
- **Hour 24–72:** the composure mask sets. By the time the second surgical consult happens, Bruno is *already* the patient who reassures the surgeon, who asks technical questions, who frames the prognosis in language that protects everyone else in the room from having to feel anything about it.

**What he does not do, ever, in the canon, in connection with this injury:**

- Cry on-page.
- Blame Kamala on-page.
- Discuss the injury with Kamala in language that names what it costs him.
- Accept a single offered apology without redirecting it.
- Refer to the hand as "my hand." (He says "the hand," "this," "it.")

**What he does do:**

- Adopts a brace, then a glove, by month two. The glove becomes a permanent costume element; it is also functional cover for the visible atrophy and the brace beneath.
- Switches to verbal direction of others' hands in shared lab settings — a skill he develops rapidly because he is, characterologically, already a teacher.
- Re-learns to solder left-handed. Imperfectly. The joints he makes after the injury are visibly cruder; he stops making them in front of Kamala.
- Withdraws from physical proximity to Kamala by a measurable margin. Pre-injury, he routinely sits within arm's length on the Circle Q stool, the Khan couch, the school bleachers. Post-injury, he sits one seat further out. This persists.
- Begins, for the first time in the run, to *decline* requests. Small ones. The decline is always gentle, always rationalized, always plausible. The pattern is new.

**The Mike conversation** in this window — the breakup, the not-quite-confession to Kamala, the catastrophic timing — proceeds with the dreamlike inevitability of someone too tired to steer. Mike, who has seen this coming for longer than Bruno has admitted it to himself, ends it with grace. The not-quite-confession to Kamala is interrupted, then displaced, then revealed too late, then irrelevant because Kamala is — by the time the words could land — already someone else. The romantic foreclosure and the somatic foreclosure happen inside the same forty pages of canon. He files them together, because there is only one drawer.

---

## VI. THE INTERREGNUM — WHAT HE DOES WITH HIMSELF *(Ms. Marvel 2015 #13–17)*

There is a stretch of issues — short, narratively crowded with other plot — in which Bruno is on-page but functionally absent. He attends. He builds. He answers questions. He does not initiate. This is the closest the canon comes to depicting his depressive trough, and it is depicted by *absence* — fewer panels, fewer lines, fewer expressions, the artists drawing him with the eyes one notch more downcast and the mouth one notch more closed.

**Sub-threshold adjustment-disorder behaviors in this window:**

- Sleep onset latency increases; on multiple background panels he is shown awake at the workbench at hours that exceed his pre-injury norm. The work itself slows. He spends longer on tasks he used to clear in an hour.
- He eats less. Muneeba Khan, in one quiet panel, puts a plate in front of him without saying anything and watches until he picks up the fork.
- He stops folding the receipt paper at the register. (Hands have changed their relationship to small motor habits.)
- He takes the long route home. The standard Circle Q → home walk is replaced by a longer perimeter that passes the Hudson waterfront and adds twenty minutes. He does this most nights for several weeks. The function is unclear in canon; the inference is the obvious one — he is not ready to be inside walls.

He does not seek help. He does not name what is happening. He completes the school semester with grades that do not slip enough for anyone to notice. He is, by any external measure, *fine*. The longitudinal record disagrees and the record is correct.

---

## VII. WAKANDA — THE DECISION, THE TRANSIT, THE FIRST YEAR *(Ms. Marvel 2015 #18–19 and bridging issues, 2017)*

The Wakanda transfer is the largest single behavioral discontinuity in the longitudinal record. It is also, characteristically, the least *discussed*. He is offered an academic placement at the Wakandan science academy — credentials, opportunity, the kind of pedigree that resolves a working-class Jersey City kid's whole financial future at one stroke. The opportunity is real. The escape is also real. He takes it and the canon refuses to let him pretend either reading is the whole story.

**The decision sequence:**

1. **Internal latency:** a stretch of issues in which the offer is in his pocket and he does not mention it.
2. **Triangulated disclosure:** he tells Mike before he tells Kamala. He tells Bruno's lab teacher before he tells his parents. He tells Vick last among the people who matter and first among the people he is responsible for, which is the correct order by his internal logic and emotionally backwards by everyone else's.
3. **The conversation with Kamala:** brief, technical, framed as opportunity. She protests. He does not argue. He does not soften. He does not stay.
4. **Departure:** quiet, off-page, without a party.

**First year in Wakanda — observable adjustments:**

- New circuit, new rhythm. Lab access is functionally unlimited; he uses it. His sleep improves measurably (depicted indirectly by the artists in fewer under-eye shadows). He gains a small amount of weight. He stands straighter.
- **Kareem.** The Red Dagger relationship develops in this window. The canon is tasteful about timeline and tactful about intensity; the relevant pattern is that Bruno, for the first time in the longitudinal record, *enters a relationship in which he is not the one carrying the weight.* Kareem has his own life, his own city, his own missions; Bruno is not infrastructure to him, he is a *person*. The shift is observable in micro-tells: Bruno laughs more in panels set in Wakanda than in any prior period; he is photographed (an in-universe holo) leaning back rather than forward; he initiates contact rather than waiting for it.
- He does not call Kamala first. He answers when she calls. The asymmetry that defined Jersey City inverts; in Wakanda, *she* is the one who has to reach.
- He works on Wakandan problems, not Ms. Marvel problems. He builds nothing for her in this window. The lab discipline of not-building-for-her is, internally, a kind of mourning.

**What does not change:**

- He still does not discuss the hand. Wakandan medical technology is the most advanced on the planet and the canon pointedly does not show him pursuing reconstruction. He could. He doesn't. The reading is that the hand has become *load-bearing identity* — to fix it would be to admit it was broken, and admission is the one move his structure does not allow.
- He still does not weaponize. Visits home are warm; he does not punish Kamala by withholding warmth. He punishes her — if punishment is even the word, and it probably isn't — only by being *somewhere else now*, which was never legible as punishment to him because to him it was survival.

---

## VIII. THE RETURNS — RECALIBRATING THE BOND *(Wilson late run, 2018)*

Bruno comes back to Jersey City repeatedly in this window. Short visits, longer ones, the eventual functional re-residence by the end of Wilson's tenure. Each return is a small recalibration and the cumulative effect is the *professionalization* of the friendship.

**Markers of the recalibration:**

- **Greeting pattern:** pre-Wakanda, Kamala hugged him on sight without thinking. Post-Wakanda, there is a beat — half a panel, sometimes a full panel — in which both of them check, and then the hug happens, and it is warm but it is no longer reflexive. The check is the new normal.
- **Lab collaboration resumes** but on different terms. He builds with her, not for her. He says no when he means no. He asks her to hand him things; he names the hand; he does not pretend the hand is not the reason.
- **Conversational register shifts** from intimate-personal to operational-friendly. They discuss missions. They discuss Vick. They discuss, occasionally, Kareem. They do not discuss the warehouse. They do not discuss what almost was. By tacit mutual treaty, those subjects are closed.
- **He becomes the adult-coded friend.** Where pre-injury he was the *competent peer*, post-Wakanda he is something subtly different — the friend who has lived a little further out, who has a partner, who has a job-shaped life, who provides perspective rather than infrastructure. He is, at seventeen or eighteen, already *older* than his cohort in a way that will only widen.

---

## IX. THE VICK SUBPLOT, ONGOING *(distributed through middle period)*

Through the entire middle period, Vick is the constant subliminal load. He is in and out of trouble; in and out of school; in and out of legitimate work. Bruno's relationship to Vick is the rehearsal space for every other relational pattern he runs. With Vick he is parent, banker, lawyer-by-proxy, and the one who shows up at the precinct at 23:00 on a school night. The Wakanda transfer creates the first real test of whether the Carrelli family system can hold without Bruno in physical residence, and the canon depicts, in restrained beats, both that it *partially can* (Vick stabilizes incrementally, perhaps because Bruno is no longer available as the safety net) and that Bruno *does not entirely believe this* (he calls Vick from Wakanda more often than he calls anyone else).

**Pattern crystallized in this window:** Bruno's caretaking, when given distance, does not stop — it *redirects* into the form least visible to its recipient (long-distance financial and logistical support, the wired tuition, the rent absorbed, the quiet phone call to a probation officer he should not be calling). The shape of his love is irreducibly *infrastructural*. Geography does not change the shape, only the channel.

---

## X. THE WAR-ADJACENT PERIOD AND THE QUIET WAR INSIDE

Across the middle period Bruno is adjacent to multiple capital-E Events — the Inventor's labor war, Civil War II, various Inhumans-vs.-X-Men proximate skirmishes, the Last Days material near *Secret Wars*. He fights in none of them as a principal. He is in *all* of them as the person who built the thing that worked.

**His war is internal and it has three fronts:**

1. **The romantic foreclosure**, which closes in the warehouse and is never reopened. He grieves it by not naming it. The grief is metabolized into Kareem, into Wakanda, into work; it does not vanish.

2. **The somatic foreclosure**, which is the hand. The hand is grieved by not being grieved. The longitudinal record is unambiguous: a person whose identity was hands, who lost the use of one, who never once spoke the loss out loud, is carrying it. He carries it by carrying it.

3. **The vocational reconstitution**, which is the *successful* front. He builds a self that is a scientist first, an inventor second, a friend third, a brother fourth, a partner fifth — and the rank order, established in this period, holds for the rest of the record. The reordering is the gift the injury made him take. He would not have ordered himself this way without it. He would have remained Kamala's infrastructure and called it a life.

---

## XI. THE END-STATE OF THE MIDDLE PERIOD

By the close of Wilson's run and the threshold of *Magnificent Ms. Marvel*, Bruno Carrelli is no longer the boy at the Circle Q register. He is a credentialed working scientist with international affiliation, a partner, a permanent injury he does not discuss, a softened-but-permanent reserve toward the person he most loved, a younger brother stabilizing at distance, parents he has functionally written out of the operational picture, and an identity reconstituted around vocation rather than around being-needed-by-Kamala.

The middle period is the arc in which he learns — through a sequence of events none of which he chose, with the conspicuous exception of Wakanda — that the version of him who built his life around one person's safety was not sustainable, not for him and arguably not for her. He does not repudiate that earlier self. He does not even mourn him visibly. He simply becomes, by small and conservative increments, *someone else who looks the same from a distance and is structurally different up close.*

**Operational summary for the file:** the middle period is when the steady one learned the precise weight of being steady. He kept being steady. The cost is in the record. He has not yet sent the bill, and the longitudinal question — the question Section 5 closes on — is what happens to a person whose reliability has never been allowed to fail, in the next period, when something finally asks him for more than even he can quietly absorb.


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

## Preamble: Scope of this section

This section covers the post-*Magnificent Ms. Marvel* window through the present-tense observational window: roughly the Saladin Ahmed late-run material, the *Beyond* arc and Kamala's "death" event (*Amazing Spider-Man* #26, 2022), the *Fallen Friend* aftermath, the *Ms. Marvel: The New Mutant* (2023) reframing, and the *X-Men*-adjacent integration that followed. The subject's footprint across this window is smaller in panel-count than in any prior era — itself a finding — and denser in *implication* per appearance than at any point since the Civil War II inflection. He has been pushed to the periphery of the social field he once anchored, has lost and re-gained the central object of his attachment under unprecedented circumstances, and has, by every indicator we can extract from the longitudinal record, completed a transition from *adolescent infrastructure* into something closer to *adult professional with a closed file on his own youth*.

What follows maps that transition in granular detail.

---

## 1. The late-Ahmed window: professionalization complete

By the closing arcs of *Magnificent Ms. Marvel* and the run-up to *Beyond*, the subject's on-page presentation has stabilized into a stable adult-coded posture that the earlier eras only gestured toward. The visual register is consistent across artists: the brace or compression glove on the right hand is now a permanent costume element rather than an episodic reminder; the silhouette has filled out marginally (shoulders broader, posture squarer); the hair has been kept at the same medium-short cut for multiple years now — a *grooming routine that has stopped changing*, which in a character whose adolescent appearances were tracked by variations in hair length is itself a marker of identity-consolidation. He is no longer trying things on.

Behavioral signatures across this window:

- **Verbal register has shifted.** Sentence lengths in his dialogue are shorter; technical terminology is offered without the prior habit of self-deprecating qualifiers ("I think," "maybe," "if I'm reading this right"). The hedge-language of the Wilson-era teenager has been quietly retired. He explains; he no longer auditions.
- **Spatial positioning in panel composition.** Across multiple artists, the subject is increasingly framed at the *edge* of group scenes — standing slightly behind Kamala's shoulder rather than beside her, leaning on a doorframe rather than crossing the threshold. This is not exclusion by the storytellers; it is a posture *he* has adopted. He stations himself where he can see the whole room.
- **Touch repertoire has contracted.** Casual physical contact with Kamala — the shoulder-bumps, the elbow-grabs, the in-panel proximities of the Wilson run — are essentially absent. When they do touch, it is purposive: hand on her arm to stop her saying something, hand passed across a workbench to deliver a tool. The intimacy register has been re-zoned from *familial* to *colleagual*.
- **The Circle Q has receded.** The convenience store that anchored the earliest Wilson visuals appears in this window only as nostalgia-staging. The subject's working spaces are now: a personal lab (post-Wakanda kit reassembled stateside), university lab benches, and Kamala's home as a tactical staging area rather than as a hang-out.

The professionalization read is not an upgrade narrative. It is a *containment* narrative. He has converted the unresolved material of the Civil War II–Wakanda axis into a stable working posture that allows him to remain in Kamala's orbit without re-opening the question that nearly broke him.

---

## 2. *Beyond* / Kamala's death (2022): the unwitnessed catastrophe
